sewer alignment

EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
The purpose of this study was to investigate the subsurface
geotechnical conditions in order to provide information on anticipated
tunneling conditions geotechnical design recommendations and
construction considerations for the Sewer Tunnel Relief Increment 2
Cartwright Field to Metcalf Street on the island of Oahu Hawaii
A multi phase exploration program was carried out which included
rilling of large 42 inch diameter observation shafts
installation of 39 piezometers or observation wells performing field
permeability grout injection and in situ electric cone penetration
tests and laboratory soil testing
The results of the geotechnical investigation indicate that the
tunnel will be constructed predominantly in uncemented to locally
cemented cinder sands and highly complex and variable zones of hard
basalt layers and boulders cinders clays and silts weathered volcanic
tuff and marine clays and coral Very difficult mixed face conditions
are anticipated along approximately one third about 1500 L F of the
proposed sewer alignment Approximately two thirds of the tunnel will
be above or near the existing ground water table The remaining
one third is anticipated to have water in the invert or perched water
table condition allowing local water in flows above the invert
The 5166 L F of 60 inch I D RCP sewer in Increment 2 is to be
placed in tunnel and open cut excavations
From Station 0 00 to 26 90 tunneling is to be accomplished using
an open face circular shield with muck removed from the Makiki Park
Shaft Tunneling will be carried out predominantly in cemented to
uncemented cinders with some silt layers The tunnel ground will range
from firm capable of standing unsupported in the tunnel face to
running where the soil displaces until it forms a slope in the tunnel
e Fae
GEOLABS HAWAIi
at its natural angle of repose to flowing where the soil is carried
into the tunnel by seepage of water that may be present in the invert or
perched on silty layers above the invert
From Station 27 80 to 41425 the City and County of Honolulu
requires that the section be tunneled The tunnel can be advanced from
either end mucking to the Makiki Park Shaft or a shaft located at the
east end of the section Through most of the section the tunnel will
be in a mixed face of soil predominantly cinder sand and marine or
tuffaceous silts and clays and rock boulders layers and masses of
basaltic rock The tunnel ground conditions will include firm
running and flowing often in combination with rock or boulders
requiring rock excavation methods such as blasting The alignment of
this section should be set so that the surface is accessible for
installing grout and drill holes and for installing a braced excavation
should it be necessary to recover the shield or complete the
excavation Progress through this section will be slow and difficult
An open face shield partial shield or no shield can be used in this
section They must have capabilities for spiling or forepoling ahead of
the face and for complete breasting of the face in order to support
running or flowing soils and also permit excavation of rock
From Station 41 25 to 51 61 the sewer can be constructed by open
cutting or tunneling Depths to the base of the excavation are less
than in the previous sections and range from approximately 28 to 16
feet Predominant in this section is a tuffaceous silt and clay
containing numerous basalt boulders and some layers of cinder sand In
some sections marine clays coral sand and gravel may be encountered
near the invert A full face of basalt will be present as the sewer
turns into the hill at Metcalf Street at the end of the section
vicinity Station 51 00
X
GEOLABS HAWAIi
Sections requiring special construction measures to control ground
movements and protect existing facilities include tunneling beneath the
Lunalilo Freeway approximately Station 5 92 to 7 46 tunneling or open
cutting beneath the existing sewer on Wilder Avenue near Punahou Street
approximately Station 27 00 to 28 00 and open cutting for passage
beneath the existing sewer at Wilder Avenue and Piper s Pali
approximately Station 41 00 to 42 00 Compaction grouting techniques
coupled with careful monitoring of ground movement are proposed to
limit settlement beneath the Lunalilo Freeway The grout will be placed
if ground movements exceed certain limits as the tunnel is advanced
beneath the freeway At the two sewer crossings the vertical distance
between the existing sewer and the proposed tunnel is only 5 to 6 feet
thus placing constraints on the options for controlling ground movements
and protecting the sewers Diversion of flow and support of the
existing sewers would be accomplished prior to installing the proposed
pipe to minimize the risk of damage to and loss of waste water from the
existing sewer
xii
GEOLABS HAWAII
GEOTECHNICAL ENGINEERING REPORT
SEWER TUNNEL RELIEF INCREMENT 2
CARTWRIGHT FIELD TO METCALF STREET
1 INTRODUCTION
This report presents information on field exploration subsurface
conditions tunneling and excavation conditions geotechnical design
recommendations and construction considerations for the Sewer Tunnel
Relief Increment 2 Cartwright Field to Metcalf Street Honolulu Oahu
Hawaii
This report was prepared for specific application to the subject
project in accordance with generally accepted geotechnical engineering
practices No other warranty expressed or implied is made While
this report is recommended for inclusion as part of the contract
document it has not been prepared as a specification
l 1
GEOLABS HAWAIi
2 PROJECT DESCRIPTION
The Sewer Tunnel Relief Increment 2 is to be located in the
Makiki area of Honolulu and is within the Mamala Bay Sewerage District
of Oahu Figures 2 1 and 2 2 When completed it will help to
alleviate the present problems of declining capacity progressive
structural degradation and maintenance difficulties faced by the
existing Manoa Kaimuki Interceptor Sewer
The tunnel is part of a project jointly supported by the City
County of Honolulu State of Hawaii and the U S Environmental
Protection Agency
The tunnel will be constructed in materials varying from
predominantly uncemented or locally cemented cinder sands to highly
complex and variable clays and silts weathered tuff boulders and
layers or masses of basalt rock cinder sand and reworked cinder sand
marine sediments and remnants of coral reefs Drawing Nos 1 to 6
In general approximately two thirds of the sewer main will be
above or near the existing ground water table The remaining one third
is anticipated to have water at the invert or perched water table
conditions allowing local water flows above the invert Drawing Nos 1
to 6
Several additional features related to tunnel construction are
discussed in this report These include braced cuts portal drop
shaft and manhole construction
2 1 Sewer Project
Increment 2 of the Sewer Tunnel Relief consists of a 60 inch I D
reinforced concrete pipe RCP sewer main In this report all cover
dimensions give distance from ground surface to assumed tunnel crown
located 2 feet above the top of the 60 inch I D pipe Originally the
proposed alignment for Increment 2 began at Makiki Street just mauka
uphill of Lunalilo Street crossed under Lunalilo Freeway and
continued along Wilder Avenue to Metcalf Street Figure 2 1

GENERAL LOCATION
2 2
CARTWRIGHT FIELD TO METCALF STREET
I Foundation Soil Hin gineering Geology
Based on the preliminary findings from this study a revised
alignment that begins at Kinau Street from the makai south side of
Cartwright Field crosses under Lunalilo Freeway continues through
Makiki Park and curves into and along Wilder Avenue to Metcalf Street
was recommended Figures 2 1 and 2 2
The western and central 4100 L F of the 5166 L F RCP sewer is a
tunnel section This section ranges from 13 to 48 feet deep to tunnel
crown The central Station 29 00 to 41400 1200 L F section shall be
constructed by tunneling but very difficult tunneling condition is
anticipated The eastern 1061 1 L F is a shallow section with 8 to 20
feet of cover over the tunnel The eastern section may involve
installation of the 60 inch RCP by the cut and cover method along Wilder
Avenue between Artesian and Metcalf Streets
Main advantages of the revised sewer alignment are
i re aligning the sewer line away from Makiki Street to
minimize the potential adverse effect of tunnel construction on
adjoining multi story buildings
ii presence of open park land Cartwright Field and Makiki
District Park at the beginning of the section allows for the monitoring
and evaluation of the performance of the contractor s tunneling method
in structurally non critical areas prior to excavating under the
Lunalilo Freeway and close to major buildings along Wilder Avenue and
iii major construction shafts and portals can be located within
the open park areas which eliminates serious disruption to traffic and
utility services
GEOLABS HAWAII
A drop shaft which will also serve as the main construction shaft
Will be constructed at about Station 16 00 The shaft will extend about
53 feet from the existing ground surface to the invert level
Eight 8 sewer manholes are to be constructed along the alignment
of the sewer main these vary in depth from 19 to 54 feet from the
existing ground surface Drawing Nos 1 to 6
The proposed sewer tunnel crosses under two important structures
the Lunalilo Freeway and the existing 4 x 5 feet sewer tunnel at two
locations The crossing beneath the freeway is approximately 154 feet
long and with cover ranging from 23 to 27 feet The new sewer tunnel
crosses about 6 feet below the existing sewer at about Station 27 00 to
28 00 under approximately 45 feet of cover beneath Wilder Avenue At
about Station 41 50 the crossing is approximately 6 feet beneath the
existing sewer under 18 feet of cover Special construction measures
Will be required to install the new sewer beneath both the Freeway and
the existing sewer tunnel while maintaining the required use of these
facilities
2 2 Site Description and Conditions
The proposed tunnel is situated in the highly developed mainly
residential Makiki area of Honolulu Hawaii The topography and various
surface features along the alignment are shown on Figures 2 1 and 2 2
and Drawing Nos 1 to 6
Topographically the project area varies in elevation from
approximately 28 to 65 feet above mean sea level
The first 1600 L F of the sewer tunnel traverses in a north south
direction along the Honolulu Plain and the remaining section traverses
west to east across the foothills of major volcanic cones in the area
GEOLABS HAWAII
Building Structures
Many highrise buildings two to four story apartments and houses
adjoin the proposed sewer alignment Figure 2 2 Several buildings are
within 10 to 35 feet of the proposed tunnel excavation Drawing Nos 1
to 6
i a portion of the 9 story Punahou View Condominium at junction
of Wilder Avenue and Punahou Street is about 35 feet from the proposed
construction
ii Street story 1551 2 story 1555 2 story
1561 4 story and 1567 3 story along Wilder Avenue between Anapuni
and Poki Streets are about 25 to 36 feet from the proposed
construction and
iii three single story houses and a 2 story apartment building in
an alley by Lunalilo Street are about 12 to 23 feet from the proposed
construction
All of the above buildings are founded on spread footings except
for a single story house by Lunalilo Street which is on stilts
26202 Utilities
Construction of the proposed sewer tunnel relief will be carried
out beneath numerous utility systems which are within the roadway
right of ways These utility systems include drainage pipe culverts
with 18 to 36 inch diameters sewer existing 4 x 5 feet tunnel and 6
to 10 inch collectors water 6 to 24 inch pipes gas 2 to 4 inch
metal pipes military communication cables and electrical traffic
GEOLABS HAWAIi
lights telephone cable and TV systems Drawing Nos 1 to 6 A 100 foot
long by 10 foot wide box culvert improved Makiki Stream crosses the
proposed tunnel alignment on Wilder Avenue at Station 20 30 about 30
feet above the proposed tunnel crown
Overhead electrical cables may restrict construction equipment and
thereby affect the construction of Sewer Manhole Nos 5 and 7
The previous and Associates study 1971 revealed
cracks separation and holes through the concrete lining of the existing
tunnels The most serious cracks and voids were observed in the crown
of the existing tunnel over much of the length along Wilder Avenue
between Piikoi and Alexander Streets Associates Inc
1971 P 24
Defects in the tunnel lining between Liholiho and Punahou Streets
were repaired by the City County of Honolulu in 1973 The repair work
involved
i installation of temporary blocking forms and post supports in
the tunnel arch to hold grout placed from the ground surface
ii drilling holes from the street surface and filling of deep
cracks in the lining by pressure grouting
iii filling voids above the initial grout layer with light weight
concrete and
iv filling drill holes up to grade with light weight concrete and
caulking of all cracks with dry packed mortar
GEOLABS HAWAII
Details of repair work are recorded on As Built Drawings Division
of Sewers Department of Public Works City County of Honolulu Job
Our inspection of the existing sewer between Punahou Street and
Piper s Pali indicates that the 1973 repair work was extended to the
east of Punahou Street by approximately 150 feet Details of the
condition of the existing sewer are presented in Appendix K
Recreational Facilities
There are three recreational and park areas along the proposed
tunnel alignment Cartwright Field Makiki District Park and Punahou
Square Makiki District Park is an open area with four tennis courts
two volleyball courts and one basketball court Cartwright Field has
areas for softball and playground equipment Punahou Square provides an
open area for passive recreation Construction of the tunnel will not
adversely disrupt any of these recreational activities
A contractor s staging area and space for shaft construction will
be located at the northeastern corner of Makiki District Park which is
operated by the Department of Parks and Recreation Drawing No 2
GEOLABS HAWAII
3 INVESTIGATION PROGRAM
3 1 Introduction
The purpose of the geotechnical engineering investigation was to
explore the subsurface conditions along the sewer alignment to provide
pertinent soil parameters to aid in the design and construction of the
proposed sewer tunnel relief
The scope of the investigation included
1 a literature review of pertinent data such as previous
reports boring logs building foundation plans available aerial
photographs and
ii a two phase detailed field exploration program that included
drilling of 41 borings installation and inspection of two 2 large
42 inch diameter observation shafts in situ field permeability tests
pump tests grout injection tests installation of piezometers
monitoring of groundwater levels in situ electric cone penetrometer
testing continuous sampling detailed logging and laboratory testing
Details of drilling equipment used sampling methods adopted and
problems encountered during site investigation are presented in Appendix
As
Boring logs field and laboratory test results are presented in
Appendices B C D E L and M of this report
GEOLABS HAWAII
3 2 Data Sources
An office study of all available pertinent data was carried out
prior to planning of the field exploration program Information on the
regional geology existing sewer alignment and conditions adjoining
buildings and other structures along the alignment and existing boring
logs were gathered and synthesized

establish the regional geology Chapter 4 0 A list of the geologic

and foundation plans of 19 buildings were obtained and studied
Foundations and building plans of older houses apartments were not
available A list of foundation plans obtained and studied is provided
in Appendix H
Previous boring logs developed for the existing sewer tunnel in
1928 and other foundation investigations in the area were obtained and
studied However these logs are not sufficiently detailed and do not
contain the pertinent information necessary for proper interpretation of
the complicated ground conditions tunnel design and construction
considerations All pertinent available information collected during
this project are available for examination at the office of
Geolabs Hawaii
As built plan on the details of repair work carried out on a
section of the existing sewer tunnel Punahou to Liholiho Streets was
provided by the Division of Wastewater Management City County of
Honolulu
Subsequent to the office study a detailed field exploration
program was planned to investigate the subsurface conditions and to
provide pertinent soil parameters for the design and construction of the
sewer tunnel relief and related structures

3 3 Project Exploratory Program
The field exploration program consisted of the following
i Inspection of surface exposures to confirm the regional
geology of the project area
ii Initial Phase I test borings sampling installation of
piezometers and in situ permeability testings in 20 locations to
delineate the general soil conditions along the proposed sewer
alignment In situ electric cone penetration tests 1 and 2 were
carried out in two selected locations Figure 2 1 Drawing Nos 2 and 5
iii Twenty one 21 additional Phase II borings to
a better define ground water conditions and contact zones of
geologic units that are pertinent to tunnel design and construction and
b install observation wells and carry out pump and grout
injection tests
iv Installation and inspection of two 2 large 42 inch
diameter observation shafts Phase II to provide ground condition and
behavior data for design and construction Windows and ladders were
constructed on shaft casings and the shafts were left open to allow
observation by prospective contractors see Appendix L
Location of Phases I and II Borings
Most of the 20 Phase I borings were placed 250 to 500 feet apart
and in general are close to shafts manholes and stream locations
3 4
GEOLABS HAWAIl
Selected Phase I borings were closely spaced 60 feet apart at
critical areas such as at Drawing Nos 1 to 6
i the main shaft C location Boring Nos G 5 and G 6
ii Makiki Stream Boring Nos G 7 G 8 and G 9 and
iii cross over of existing and proposed sewer tunnel Boring Nos
G 1l and G 12
The twenty one 21 additional Phase II borings were drilled at
selected locations Drawing Nos 1 to 6 to
i better define complicated geologic contacts boulder and rock
ii investigate ground conditions along the revised alignment
iii install observation wells and carry out pump and grout
Continuous Sampling Methods
Continuous sampling procedures were adopted for most of the borings
in this study to provide a continuous log of the subsurface and to
ensure adequate sampling of geologic units particularly at and near the
tunnel level This procedure is necessary because of
3 5
GEOLABS HAWAITi
i the complex stratigraphy expected in a volcanic alluvial
marine sequence along the alignment of the proposed sewer
ii the importance of detailed lithological variations such as
the interbedding of cinder sands and weathered tuff clayey silt on the
consideration of groutability of the subsurface and practical dewatering
procedures
iii the need to realistically identify boulder zones and
mixed face conditions at the proposed tunnel level and
iv the need to identify potential perched water conditions near
and at the proposed tunnel level
Continuous sampling was carried out mostly by alternate use of ring
and split spoon samplers In selected borings a Triefus Triple tube
core barrel or the Wireline HQ rock coring system were used The
Triefus Triple tube core barrel was used to recover rock boulders and
cemented soils The Triple tube results were correlated with Standard
Penetration resistances obtained during split spoon sampling in adjacent
holes or layers
Details of drilling and sampling methods and equipment used are
described in Appendix A of this report
Piezometers and Field Permeability
Field permeability Falling Head tests were carried out to
determine the in situ hydraulic conductivity of the interbedded cinder
sand and tuff and coral units The laboratory method was not used
because of the anticipated large difference in vertical versus
horizontal permeability in the field
GEOLABS HAWAI
Thirty two 32 Falling Head tests were carried out in 20 borings
Test conditions and results are summarized in Appendix Cc
Pump tests were performed in a 42 inch diameter observation shaft
at Station 33 00 Test methods and results are summarized in Appendix C
Plates c 55 to c 59
Thirty nine 39 piezometers were installed in 35 boreholes to
allow long term monitoring of groundwater levels This is particularly
important as the field exploration was carried out during a relatively
dry period see Appendix J and groundwater response to extreme
rainstorm conditions along the tunnel alignment cannot be assessed based
on the relatively short monitoring period
Multi level piezometers were installed in Boring Nos G 12 G 13
G 14 and G 27 to monitor the probable presence of perched water
conditions
Details of piezometer installations are presented in Appendix D
Field Electric Cone Penetrometer Tests
Cone penetrometer tests 1 and 2 were carried out in two selected
locations Boring Nos G 4a and G 17a The cone penetrometer was used
because of the difficulties anticipated in obtaining undisturbed sample
of the loose and or uncemented cinder sand
The use of Mennard Pressuremeter was originally planned to provide
in situ soil deformation data on the cinder sand However the uncased
section of borings in the cinder sand seldom stand up unsupported to
allow the insertion of the pressuremeter and therefore the
hydraulically pushed electric cone penetrometer was used instead
GEOLABS HAWAI
The values of the tip resistance and friction ratio sleeve
friction over tip resistance were correlated to soil strength and
classification Comparision of such in situ test data with laboratory
tested core samples obtained by the Triefus Triple tube core barrel and
ring sampler was carried out Results are presented in Appendices and
F of this report
Grout Injection Tests
Grout injection tests were carried out in Boring Nos G 34 and
G 39 The injection of cement grout was used to provide information on
the groutability of the soils between approximate Station 28 00 and
41 00 which is required to be tunneled The test grouting was also
used to establish the suitability of grouting beneath the existing sewer
at the crossing location Station 27 00 and Sewer Manhole No 7
foundation Station 41 00
Details of test method and results are presented in Appendix M
Laboratory Testing
Pertinent laboratory tests were carried out to determine the
engineering properties of geologic materials encountered during field
investigation The moisture content unit weight and Atterberg Limits
of selected samples were determined Sieve analyses were performed on
samples of cinder sand to aid in classification and for consideration of
grouting techniques
Unconfined compression tests and the direct shear tests were
carried out to determine soil strength parameters
Swell tests were carried out on weathered tuff clayey silt to
silty clay and marine clay samples to evaluate the swelling potential
and pressures of these geologic units
GEOLABS HAWAIl
Unconfined compression Scleroscope and abrasive hardness tests
and the Schmidt hammer test were performed by the University of Illinois
to provide rock strength and hardness data
Details of laboratory test results are presented in Appendix E

GEOLABS HAWAII
4 GENERAL GEOLOGIC SETTING
4 1 Geologic History
Oahu the third largest of the eight major islands of the Hawaiian
Archipelago covers a land area of approximately 604 square miles The
island was formed by the volcanic activity of two large shield shaped
volcanoes
The entire Hawaiian Archipelago forms a southeast trending line of
volcanic islands 1491 miles long The major Hawaiian Islands are
located along a 404 mile line at the southeasterly end of the chain
The island of Oahu is divided into four main areas The Waianae
Range The Koolau Range The Schofield Plateau and The Coastal Plains
The chief topographic features of the island of Oahu are the two
elongated basaltic domes Waianae Range on the west side and the Koolau
Range on the east side The Schofield Plateau is located where the two
ranges merge The Coastal Plains adjacent to the ocean are nearly level
and lie on the ponded lavas of the Koolau Volcano The Honolulu Plain
extends easterly from Pearl Harbor and is mostly occupied by the City of
Honolulu and Waikiki
The Koolau Volcanic Shield was built during the late Pliocene and
early Pleistocene by thin bedded basaltic lava flows from a rift zone
that roughly parallels the existing mountain trends The main Koolau
Shield building activity ended approximately 2 5 million years ago
The project site is located within the Manoa Makiki District which
lies on the southern flank of the Koolau Range that forms the
southeastern portion of Oahu Figures 2 1 and 4 1

The stratigraphic history of the Manoa Makiki area is quite
complex due to its areal extent the complex series of sea level changes
and the secondary volcanic activity that is superimposed on the
topography of the Koolau Range
Evidence from drilled wells indicates that the island of Oahu has
subsided up to 1200 feet since the cessation of the Koolau Volcanic
activity
During that period of subsidence extensive growth of coral reefs
and accumulation of interbedded terrigenous sediments occurred along the
southern coast of Oahu
During the Pleistocene Ice Age there were many sea level
changes The higher sea level stands caused the accumulation of reef
deposits at corresponding higher elevations The lower sea stands
caused streams to carve valleys through the sediments and reef deposits
When the sea stood about 40 feet higher than the present level a
long line of sea cliffs were cut along the southern coast During this
time gravel terraces and fans were built at the base of the cliffs by
the streams that cut through these cliffs
After a period of repose a new period of volcanism began in the
southeast portion of the Koolau Range Although these eruptions were
small compared to the major volcanic activity of the main Koolau dome
more than 30 separate eruptions formed cinder ash spatter cones and
poured lava flows over the eroded topography and onto some of the
fringing coral reefs This period of post erosional volcanism known as
the Honolulu Volcanic Series spanned about one half million years
roughly from mid Pleistocene to Recent
Of the 30 separate eruptions about 6 to 7 have affected the study
area
4 3
GEOLABS HAWAII
4 2 Volcanic Rocks
The following secondary volcanic events associated with the
project area are summarized in the order they occurred
Punchbowl Volcanics
The Punchbowl tuff cone located about one mile west of the site
erupted during the Waipio Low Stand 350 of the sea
The Punchbowl cone building eruption was rather explosive
Phreatomagmatic in nature owing to the interaction of groundwater with
the rising magma as it penetrated a coral reef resulting in the
expulsion of large quantities of pyroclastic materials such as ash and
cinders These deposits have consolidated to form tuff The later
eruptions of Punchbowl were purely magmatic and did not involve large
amounts of steam and subsequently resulted in lava flows rather than
pyroclastic airborne eruptions Some lava rose into the crater Much
later black glassy ash from the Tantalus Group covered the interior of
the crater and easterly flank Possibly some ash from the Punchbowl
eruption may be encountered at the western edge of the site in the
interbedded cinder and tuff sequence
Rocky Hill Volcanics
Rocky Hill is a cinder and spatter cone located just northeast of
Punahou School that is partly buried with later pyroclastics and lava
flows from the later Sugarloaf Roundtop and Tantalus eruptions
Four other craters belonging to the Rocky Hill Group lie from
one fourth to three fourths of a mile in a northeasterly to
southeasterly direction from Rocky Hill
4 4
GEOLABS HAWAITI
An old well on the south slope below Rocky Hill encountered sand
and coral at 25 feet elevation resting on Rocky Hill Lava Therefore
lava from the Rocky Hill craters probably was emplaced prior to the
Kaena Stand 95 to 100 of the sea
The lava flow from Rocky Hill was extruded in an extremely viscous
condition that shows some flow structure with nodular lumps that were
fused and later turned into deposits of detrital agglomerate
At about elevation 100 on the south side of Rocky Hill and Punahou
School a spring issues a steady flow of water The water is probably
perched above by a lower permeability layer in the permeable Rocky Hill
deposits
Roundtop Sugarloaf and Tantalus vents follow along a north south
trending ridge north of Rocky Hill and the sewer line These three
cinder cones were formed by strombolian type eruptions and are
responsible for much of the black cinder sand in the Makiki area
Roundtop appears to be older than the other two vents
Well bedded cinder is exposed along the road cuts of Roundtop Drive
The coarse cinder contains dense spherical probably bombs formed
during venting and then spewed out of the crater
Sugarloaf and Tantalus are both about the same age and very
young less than 70 000 years ago The cinder products from both vents
are mixed together Both produced lava flows The lava from Sugarloaf
flowed out the east side of the cone and down in a southerly direction
covering the lower portion of Manoa Valley and into Moiliili It rests
on limestone of the Waimanalo Stand of the Sea near the mouth of Manoa
Valley This flow probably buried portions of the Rocky Hill Group
GEOLABS HAWAII
The lava flow from Tantalus flowed westerly into upper Pauoa
Valley
The cinders from the Tantalus Group of craters form a highly
permeable porous cap for intake of rainwater Most of this water
appears to be perched water bodies that sometime reach the surface
downslope as springs
4 3 Sediments
Intermediate Marine Sediments
These are formations deposited after the great erosion period but
older than reef formations and basalt deposits associated with recent
stands of the sea
Large amounts of pyroclastic material and terrigenous sediments
have been deposited under marine and alluvial conditions Because the
overall permeability of these marine and alluvial sediments is much
lower than the underlying basalts they greatly retard the seaward
movement of groundwater and are commonly referred to as caprock
Gravel and clay layers in an unoxidized condition are gray in
color probably of submarine deposition
Recent Alluvium
These include the terrestrial sediments deposited by the movement
of water Most are fine grained and well graded Some are uniformly
graded gravel with cobbles Along the project length the recent
alluvial sediments appear to be fairly shallow and grade into the
weathered surfaces of the volcanic tuff or ash deposits

5 SUBSURFACE CONDITIONS ALONG PROPOSED SEWER ALIGNMENT
an
el Introduction
Subsurface conditions and soil properties were determined by
sampling field testing observation classification and laboratory
testing of samples which were collected using several exploratory boring
methods see Chapter 3 Soil properties are generalized in discussions
within the text of this report For specific details we recommend
examination of the appropriate boring logs see Appendix A and
laboratory test data see Appendix E Field logs and most of the
samples collected during this project except those destroyed during
testing are available for examination through arrangement with the
Division of Wastewater Management City County of Honolulu Potential
bidders are advised of the above through notification within the bid
documents
Geologic units found to occur along the proposed sewer alignment
are
a Recent MUDFLOW and ALLUVIUM Deposits gravelly clay CH
gravelly clayey silt MH and gravelly sand all with cobbles and
boulders
b Weathered TUFF primarily clayey silt MH some clay CH
with gravel cobbles and boulders fissured in places In local areas
the tuff is fused and unweathered
c Interbedded CINDERS and weathered or reworked TUFF silty sand
gravelly sand SP to sandy gravel interbedded with thin
layers of silt to gravelly sandy silt The cinder sands are generally
loose to dense and are uncemented to locally slightly cemented or
cemented
Gd BASALT flows very dense hard to vesicular basalts with
broken and clinker zones
GEOLABS HAWAII
e Marine CLAY clayey silt MH and clay CH with gravel to
boulder sized inclusions fissured in places and
f CORAL sandy silt sandy gravel to hard coral and cavities
Generally the first 2900 L F about Station 0 00 to 29 00 of
the proposed sewer traverses across the higher elevations of the
Honolulu Plain The stratigraphy here is relatively simple comprised
of three basic geologic units of alluvium cinder sand with or without
weathered or reworked tuff interbeds and marine clay The cinder sand
unit is typically 40 to 50 feet thick and is deposited on a relatively
flat basal marine clay or coral surface Alluvium weathered tuff and
mudflow deposits overlie the cinder sand
The remaining portion approximately 2300 L F about Station
29 00 to of the proposed sewer crosses along the southerly
flank of Rocky Hill an extinct volcanic cone where complex
interbeddings of cinders tuff basalt flows marine clay and coral
units exist
Several geologic processes probably reworked and or deposited the
geologic materials at the same time volcanic activity was taking place
north of the alignment These processes include
i Reworking of black cinder by wave action and deposition in a
near shore marine environment
ii Deposition of relatively thick 20 feet layers of weathered
tuff ejecta up to 3 feet in size and spatter scoria from local vents
iii Basalt lava flows
GEOLABS HAWAII
iv Fluvial mudflow and colluvial deposition of cinder tuff and
basalt blocks on the coastal plain
These processes have resulted in complex stratigraphic and
lithologic sequences along the eastern half of the proposed alignment
Between approximate Station 29 00 to ground conditions are
expected to vary over short distances and between borings Thus the
actual ground conditions are anticipated to be much more complicated than
those shown on Drawing Nos 3 to 6 and in the detailed description
below Between approximate Station 0 00 to 29 00 the cinder sections
appear to be more uniform
5 2 Reach 1 Approximate Station 00 00 to 10 00
Kinau Street to Makiki Park
Borings encountered three basic geologic units
i Surficial recent unconsolidated sediments mudflow and alluvium
ii Cinder sand unit with weathered and reworked tuff interbeds
iii Basal marine clay
The uppermost mudflow and alluvial unit generally consist of brown
to dark brown gravelly silty clay with some fine sand Locally lenses
of sand and gravel with some cobbles exist in now buried stream channel
deposits Boring Nos G 5 G 2 and G 22
Standard penetration test SPT N values vary from 10 to 25
blows foot for the silty clay pocket penetrometer values Pp of 5 0 to
6 5 ks and N values in the gravelly sand and cobbles range from over
30 blows foot to refusal 50 blows 0 5 foot
5 3
GEOLABS HAWAII
Beneath the surficial deposits is a thick up to 45 feet cinder
sand and weathered or reworked tuff sequence The cinder sand is
commonly black to brown in color but is reddish brown where it is
oxidized near the water table The cinder sand is predominantly a
uniformly graded gravelly medium to coarse sand with traces of silt
However local increases in silt fine sand or gravel content are common
zones of cemented cinder sand were encountered in the borings and
are typically a few inches to 3 feet thick Cementation layers generally
occur in the middle and near the bottom of the unit Lateral extent of
the cemented cinder is not known Standard penetration test N values
for cemented cinders are generally greater than 40 blows foot
Particle size distribution curves showing the grain sizes Cinder
Sand ranges are presented in Appendix E
Between approximate Station 0 00 and 10 00 brown clayey silt to
gravelly sandy silt weathered tuff layers 1 to 12 inch thickness are
commonly interbedded with the cinder sand Photograph 1 1 The contact
between the silty layer and the cinders are often gradational and dip
from 0 to 40 degrees The silty zones appear to be discontinuous and
cannot be correlated from one boring to another
The cinder sand is thinly bedded and the bedding planes are often
zones of weakness within cemented horizon
The effects of cinder sand gripping the 4 inch casing Boring No
G 4 Appendix A at or beneath the water table indicates that certain
portions of the cinder deposits are uncemented in situ
Beneath the interbedded cinder and volcanic tuff sequence is the
basal marine clay unit Photograph 1 2 The top of the marine clay is
at about elevation 6 feet at the north end of Makiki Park and slopes
seaward down to minus one foot and minus eight feet at the Boring Nos

5 3 Reach 2 Approximate Station 10 00 to 29 00
Makiki Park to Punahou Street
The subsurface condition along this section of the alignment is
in general similar to that in the Kinau Street to Makiki Park Section
Approximate Station 0 00 to 10 00
However the presence of Makiki Stream has resulted in shallow
erosion of the cinder sand unit and the deposition of at least 23 feet
of alluvium The alluvium consists mainly of interbedded sandy to
clayey silt and cobbly to gravelly sand The actual bottom of the
Makiki Stream channel is not known however the deeper part of the
channel is about 25 feet above the crown of the proposed sewer tunnel at
Station 20 75 Boring No G 7 It is possible that the stream channel
could be deeper between borings but does not appear to encroach into
the proposed tunnel
For a depth of 4 to 13 feet standard penetration test values for
the alluvium are low 10 to 15 blows foot but are slightly higher 20
to 35 blows foot from depths of 13 to 20 feet
A 3 to 5 foot thick zone of cemented cinder sand appears to occur
at or near the basal portion of the unit Boring Nos G 7 G 8 and
G 9 SPT N values for the cemented cinder sand commonly varies

Samples of the cinder sand recovered in the Standard Penetration
Test and ring drive samplers see Appendix A and H size Triefus
Triple tube core barrel are generally uncemented In uncemented cinder
the standard penetration N values generally range from 10 to 30
blows foot depending on in situ density and grain sizes
The degree of cementation is difficult to determine by just
inspection of samples obtained by driving split spoon or ring sampler
into the ground The apparent lack of cementation may be the result of
sampling disturbance particularly for cinders that are only slightly
cemented or which cementation is not derived from a substantial quantity
of cementing material infilling the void space Although cinder sections
exposed along road cuts in the Roundtop area north of the project are
weakly cemented and steeply standing these cinders are closer to the
vents and were deposited above sea level Based on the regional geology
see Chapter 4 the cinder ash sequence between Station 00 00 and 10 00
is likely to be deposited on a near shore marine or coastal plain
environment where reworking by waves and fluvial processes are possible
and there the cinder sand are likely to be uncemented in situ

Wilder Avenue Punahou to west of Alexander Streets
Bast of Punahou Street the ground conditions change from a
relatively uniform sequence of Recent Sediments Cinders and Tuff and
Marine Clay to highly complex soil and rock conditions Moreover
mixed face tunneling is anticipated throughout much of the section
Drawing Nos 4 and 5
Along this section of the alignment the surficial material
consists of a 2 to 4 foot thick layer of alluvium silty sand and sandy
silt
Beneath the alluvium is a 7 to 17 foot thick layer of weathered
and reworked volcanic tuff clayey silt MH that contains some pumice
cinders and gravel to boulder size blocks of rock The tuff was
encountered in all of the borings drilled along this section of the
alignment Photographs 2 and N values for this
weathered and reworked tuff unit ranges from about 15 to 43 blows foot
Frequently the advance of the drive samplers was obstructed by the
presence of cobbles and boulders ejecta within the brown clayey silt
matrix
The upper tuff is underlain by a laterally and vertically complex
seguence of volcanic cinder and tuff deposits marine sediments and
numerous basaltic lava flows This complex sequence makes up most of the
materials in the tunnel intervals see Drawing Nos 4 and 5

The geologic complexities appear to be related to the presence of
local Rocky Hill volcanic cones in a marine coastal environment that
has experienced several fluctuations in sea level Between approximate
Station 29 00 and 35 00 the thick up to 40 feet cinder sand deposit
appears to interfinger with marine sediments 4 to over 12 feet thick
and weathered tuff units and pinches out at the southern edge of Rocky
Hill about Station 35 00
The basal marine sediments were dissected subsequent to deposition
and a drop in sea level and erosional depressions were in filled by
basalt flows most likely from the Rocky Hill cones Two major lava
flows minimum 10 to 18 feet thick and numerous thinner flows about 2
to 4 feet thick were encountered during the field investigation
The results of the multi phased exploratory program reveal that the
subsurface ground conditions vary considerably between borings and over
very short distances Correlations between exploratory boreholes east of
Station 29 00 are extremely tenuous
All nine 9 borings drilled along this section of the alignment
encountered boulders Hard basalt boulders with minimum dimension of 1
to 2 feet were frequently encountered within the weathered tuff unit
Cobbles and or boulders were also encountered within both the cinder and
marine sediment units
Highly variable mixed face conditions are anticipated at the tunnel
level Conditions are likely to range from an entire face of cinder sand
to a complex sequence of cinders and marine sediments to marine
sediments basalt flows and cinder Other combinations of soils and
rocks with large variations in material properties are expected

GEOLABS HAWAI
At or near the tunnel level SPT N values for the cinder sand
varied from 12 to 47 blows foot and the sand is uncemented to locally
cemented Photographs 3 4 and N values for the marine
sediments mainly clayey silt MH some clay CH with gravel cobbles
and boulders varied from 27 to 37 blows foot Photographs 3 6 and 3 7
Pocket penetrometer unconfined compressive strength Pp in the marine
clayey silt ranged from 6 5 to
Lava flows encountered during field investigation were typically
slightly weathered to fresh dense to vesicular basalt Photographs 3 8
and 3 9 Clinker and broken zones and brown silty clay seams of up to 6
inches thick were also present in the basalt flows
Since basalt flows tend to follow any pre existing topographic
irregularities test borings carried out in 50 to 200 feet spacings
provide only limited information on the occurrence of the units Other
flows not intersected by the borings should be anticipated
Test borings carried out along this section of the proposed
alignment only provide an indication of the highly complex tunneling
conditions in an east west direction across the foothill of Rocky Hill
The three dimensional variation in ground conditions particularly in a
mauka makai uphill downhill direction has not been investigated
Should the sewer alignment be changed additional exploratory work would
be required
The large diameter test shaft CH 2 drilled at Station 33 00
confirmed that many of the thin basalt samples and cores encountered in
the 4 to 6 inch diameter test borings were lava flows see Appendix L
Moreover two flows of massive to broken basalt were encountered in the
shaft with the lower flow at tunnel level Figure 5 1 The shaft also
revealed that the cinder sand above the upper flow was weakly cemented
unsaturated and stable on the vertical shaft walls

Since cementation in the cinder sand is highly variable the cinder
encountered in the shaft above the basalt should not be assumed to be
representative of all of the intermediate level cinder along this section
of the alignment Saturated cinder and clinker zones below the basalt
were unstable during excavation
5 5 Reach 3 Approximate Station 35 00 to 38 00 Wilder Avenue
Mixed face tunneling is also expected throughout this section of
the sewer alignment Stratigraphic units along this portion of the
alignment include
i probable occurrence of a local volcanic spatter and cinder
cone about Station 34 50 to 36 50
ii basalt lava flow s interlayered with tuff and cinder volcanic
ejecta sequences about Station 35 00 to 39 00
iii possible wave eroded bluff and wave cut platform in marine
sediments which were later buried by locally wave reworked cinder
deposits about Station 35 00 to 37 00 and
iv a buried channel at and near Station 38 00 area
Five 5 borings were drilled within this 300 L F section of the
alignment and all borings encountered cobbles boulders and basaltic
lava flows Boulders were found in weathered tuff marine sediments and
cinder units
At the tunnel level mixed face conditions will include
associations of marine sediment and basalt flow s and or boulders
cinders and reworked cinders
5 18
GEOLABS HAWAII
The buried channel encountered in Boring No G 29 about Station
38 00 occurs at and beneath the invert of the proposed tunnel
excavation The former channel is infilled with cinders tuff and
basalt flows However the presence of basalt flows within and one
diameter above the proposed tunnel level on both sides of the buried
possible for water bearing inclined basalt lava flows to intersect the
tunnel along this section of the alignment The basalt flows at higher
elevation appear to have flowed downward in the buried channel from Rocky
Hill
Because cinder deposits tuffs and basalt flows often follow small
stream beds or local topography it should be expected that basalt flows
will be encountered in the tunnel at depths that are quite variable and
in isolated zones that have not been penetrated by the borings which are
spaced approximately 70 to 120 feet apart Thus conditions should be
expected to be even more variable than shown by the borings
At or near the proposed tunnel excavation level the cinder sand is
commonly uncemented to locally slightly cemented and frequently contains
cobbles of scoria SPT N values varied from 51 to 91 blows foot The
weathered volcanic tuff to over SPT N 21 to 58
blows foot and marine clay to SPT N 10 to 19
blows foot are locally fissured and slickensided Where the marine clay
is in contact with a water bearing unit such as cinder near the invert
level in Boring No G 16 the sand and clay interface are loose or soft
and wet
At Boring No G 29 the weathered tuff near the invert of the
tunnel is locally wet and very soft The tuff was probably softened by
groundwater from the cinder sand unit west of the area See Boring G 16
and or from water in the porous basalt in the buried channel beneath the
unit

5 6 Reach 4 Approximate Station 38 00 to 45 00 Wilder Avenue
The subsurface condition along this section of the alignment differ
from the previous section because of the presence of alluvial mudflow
and coralline deposits
The alluvial mudflow unit up to 12 feet thick typically occurs
beneath a surfical layer of weathered tuff and locally beneath a pocket
about Station 38 00 to 40 50 of cinder sand and gravel Photographs 4 1
and 4 2 Between approximate Station 38 00 to 43 00 the mudflow
deposit consists mainly of an interbedded sequence of gray to brown
clayey to sandy silt with rounded gravel with 3 to 6 foot thick
alluvial layer of tan gravelly silty sand SPT N values between 17 to
48 blows foot to cobbles and gravel in clayey silt matrix SPT N
values between 20 to 60 blows foot Basalt flows and boulders 1 to
5 foot thick are present in the sequence The base of the
alluvial mudflow unit occurs near or within the crown of the proposed
tunnel excavation
Beneath the alluvial mudflow unit and within the proposed
excavation is a 3 to 7 foot thick cinder sand This cinder sand appears
The cinder unit consists of very loose to locally cemented black
gravelly sand SPT N 4 to 52 blows foot that occurs between
elevations between 9 to 18 feet which coincide with one of the higher
sea level stands see Chapter 4 The cinder lens was probably reworked
by wave action along a buried black sand beach
The basalt encountered in Boring G 18 is slightly weathered hard
very dense and jointed

GEOLABS HAWATI
Overview
The different geologic units within the project area make up a
variable and complex aquifer aquitard system Groundwater recharge
predominantly occurs from precipitation falling on the uphill areas north
of the proposed tunnel The existing sewer tunnel is probably leaking
and is believed to also contribute to groundwater recharge particularly
between Punahou Street and Alexander Street The regional groundwater
flow direction is generally from north to south towards the sea
All groundwater data recorded and discussed in this report were
obtained during a low rainfall period Appendix J Based on thicknesses
of oxidation zones in the cinder sand and other historical groundwater
data groundwater table levels are expected to be much higher minimum 5
feet during wetter seasonal periods
Kinau Street to north of Lunalilo Freeway
Groundwater was observed within the cinder sand and interbedded
the groundwater level consistently occurred about 5 feet above sea level
or 1 to 4 feet beneath the proposed tunnel invert during the field
investigation At the northern end of the section the impermeable
marine clay unit is about 12 feet below sea level Boring No G 21 The
other borings were drilled well below invert but not deep enough to
intersect the clay
At Boring No G l a 1 2 feet rise in groundwater level was
recorded immediately after two days of heavy rain The water level
change indicates that the cinder sand unit is permeable and responds
rapidly to recharge from precipitation
5 26
GEOLABS HAWAII
Since the cinder sand unit allows rapid recharge from
precipitation it is likely that the thin clayey silt weathered tuff
interbeds will perch water in the cinder during or shortly after heavy
rainstorms The transient perched water tables should be expected along
sections of the proposed excavation particularly between Station 0 00 to
about 30 00 Between Station 30 00 to 38 00 perched water conditions
also exist but are due to different perching conditions
Lunalilo Freeway to Wilder Avenue
Groundwater was observed in the cinder sand but at higher
elevations 7 5 to 9 5 feet than in the soils south of the Freeway
The rise in elevation of the water table corresponds with a rise in the
weathered tuff marine clay agquitard
During the 1985 to 1986 wet season November to April which was
much drier than previous years Appendix J the groundwater table was 6
inches to 1 foot below the proposed tunnel invert at Boring Nos G 5 and
G 6 locations but 6 inches above the invert at Boring No G 8
The water table between Station 0 00 to 16 00 slopes downward in a
southward direction towards the sea Drawing Nos 1 and 2
Groundwater was observed at the base of the cinder sand unit
Here the marine clay aquitard was probably eroded in past geologic time
and formed a trough like depression The groundwater table was about 4
feet below the proposed tunnel invert during the field investigation
GEOLABS HAWAI
A complex aquifer aquitard system exists between Station 24 00 and
36 06 At Boring Nos G ll and G 12 locations the marine clay is
overlain by a weathered tuff unit and the aquitard occurs at higher
elevation 9 feet The groundwater level was observed about 12 feet
above sea level or 1 foot above the invert of the proposed tunnel
At Boring No G12 where multi level piezometers were installed
the deeper piezometer placed within a marine clay with a coral sand
interbed unit shows a groundwater level about 13 feet above sea level
and indicates the possible presence of an artesian condition within the
marine clay unit Drawing No 4
Between approximate Station 31 00 to 35 00 water is perched in the
permeable flow s above the marine sediments Piezometers installed in
Boring Nos G 27 and G 41 show perched conditions in the basalt flows at
the spring line and crown of the proposed excavation
At Boring No G 16 location the aquitard is capped by a thin 1 5
feet thick layer of weathered tuff and occurs at or near the invert of
the proposed tunnel elevation 11 feet In this section a water
bearing cinder sand pocket is confined by a thick layer of weathered
tuff The contacts and hydraulic connection between the cinder sand
pocket and the porous scoria and basalt units located west of Station
35 00 is not known
Although the sand unit is only 3 feet thick it occurs between the
spring line and the invert of the proposed tunnel Groundwater level was
near the top of the unit elevation 16 feet and a 6 inch rise was
recorded after a period of overnight rains Appendices D and J

GEOLABS HAWAI
East of Boring No G 15 the lower marine clay appears to merge
with the upper weathered tuff marine clay unit and form an impermeable
aguitard at about the springline of the proposed tunnel 14 feet
Perched water exists in the scoria and cinder sandy gravel unit above
the aguitard at the crown of the proposed tunnel elevation 19 feet
Wilder Avenue and Metcalf Street
Between Stations 38 00 and 46 00 the buried cinder sand beach
overlies a coralline unit which is porous and drains the cinders layer
The groundwater table encountered in the borings was 10 feet beneath the
proposed excavation during the field investigation It is not known
whether the coralline unit is hydraulically connected to the buried
channel at Boring No G 29
From Station 46 00 to 51 61 the proposed excavation will be
carried out mainly in clayey silt or silty clay alluvium mudflow and
weathered tuff Local pockets of cinder sand exist but groundwater was
not encountered in these units during the field investigation On the
east end of the project groundwater was present 13 feet beneath the
proposed excavation within the vesicular basalt rock unit

Pump out tests performed at approximate Station 33 00 observation
shaft CH 2 indicate that the basalt flow unit there is hydraulically

6 TUNNELING CONDITIONS
The 5166 L F of 60 in I D RCP sewer on Increment 2 is to be placed in
tunnel and open cut excavations From Station 0 00 to 26 90 tunneling is
required and is to be accomplished using an open face circular shield with
muck removed from the Makiki Park Shaft
From Station 27 80 to approximately Station 41 25 the
that the section be tunneled The tunnel can be advanced from either end An
open face shield partial shield or no shield can be used in this section
They must have capabilities for spiling or forepoling ahead of the face and
for complete breasting of the face in order to support running or flowing
soils and also permit excavation of rock
From Station 41 25 to 51 61 the sewer can be constructed by tunneling
or open cutting
Special sections described later in this chapter include tunneling
beneath the Lunalilo Freeway Station 5 90 to 7 50 tunneling or open
cutting beneath the existing sewer on Wilder Avenue near Punahou Street
approximately Station 26 90 to 27 80 and tunneling or open cutting to cross
the existing sewer at Wilder Avenue and Piper s Pali after it has bean
underpinned approximately Station 41 25 to 41 60 Special measures will be
required to permit the pipe to be installed without damage to these facili
ties
6 2 Cinder Section Station 0 00 to Station 29 00
Introduction
The southern and western portions of Increment 2 will be excavated pri
marily in cinders or interbedded cinders and silt The cinder section is
divided into two reaches depending on the presence of silt layers Reach 1 is
in interbedded cinders and silt between Stations 0 00 and aporoximate Station
10 00 The second reach which contains cemented and uncemented cinder sand
lies between Stations 10 00 and 29 00 The entire cinder section will be
constructed as a tunnel except in the access shafts which will be built as
open cuts
6 1
GEOLABS HAWAII
Reach 1 Interbedded Cinder and silt
Station 0400 to Station 10 00
Reach 1 at the south and west end of Increment 2 is a 1000 ft long
section of cinders interbedded with silt layers which passes beneath the base
ball field of Cartwright Field an alley with adjacent small houses the
Lunalilo Freeway and the tennis courts in Makiki Park The depth of cover
over the excavated crown ranges between approximately 12 and 34 ft The soils
at and above sewer level are interbedded uncemented cinders and non plastic
silt Overall the materials are medium dense to dense with some thin very
dense layers in the interbedded sequence average SPT N value of 41 blows ft
within and 15 ft above the tunnel interval Near the tunnel interval the
minimum SPT N value above water level is 16 blows ft The cinder beds are
silts tend to reduce the vertical permeability of the otherwise freely
draining cinders and to develop local perched conditions A 9 to 14 ft layer
of stiff to hard brown silty clay is present above the cinders and silt and
extends to the ground surface Water levels at the time of drilling were 1 to
4 ft below tunnel invert but could be above invert level during construction
Note It is recommended that water levels be monitored regularly prior to and
during construction and that the additional data be made available to the bid
ders and selected contractor as it becomes available
The cinders and silts when dry are expected to exhibit running beha
vior and face control will be needed to advance the tunnel and to prevent
detrimental surface settlement Table 6 1
Flowing ground will be encountered if water is present in the tunnel
interval Flowing conditions occur when the material is carried into the
tunnel by groundwater whereas running conditions involve movement of essen
tially dry cohesionless materials by sliding into the tunnel Table 6 1
The borings indicate that some water is present perched on silt layers just
below the tunnel invert In addition water can occur in the tunnel interval
by an increase in the general groundwater level which at the time of this
report is 1 to 4 ft below invert If the general water level rises above

invert level preconstruction dewatering using closely spaced surface wells
will be needed along the sections passing beneath the freeway and alley In
other areas wnere perched water is encountered flowing ground conditions can
be controlled by dewatering inside the tunnel and or by using surface wells
Dewatering from inside the tunnel can be accomplished to some extent by
installing invert wells just behind the shield and by stopping to allow
drainage from the face The dewatering should be designed to prevent or mini
mize soil flow into the face between support elements or into the drains
Large loss of ground or failure of the tunnel support is likely if water and
ground inflows are not controlled The quantity of water inflow will
generally be low
Reach 2 is located beneath Makiki Park and beneath Wilder Avenue between
Makiki and Punahou Streets The tunnel crosses beneath Makiki Stream at
Station 29 50 Tunnel crown is located 39 to to 5 tunnel diameters
below the ground surface
1 Cinder Sand
Tunneling in Reach 2 will be predominantly in the cinder sands
Both cemented and uncemented zones are present The cinder sand at the tunnel
elevation is predominantly clean but some thin silt layers are present The
cinder sand is generally a coarse to medium grained sand that contains sone
silt and gravel size fractions The cinders are typically medium dense to
dense SPI N values of 20 to 50 blows ft but some loose zones were encoun
tered primarily near Makiki Stream and below the water table at other loca
tions Laboratory tests on cemented cinders have yielded unconfined
compressive strengths of more than 200 psi Based on the physical properties
and strength values the cemented cinder is properly classified as a weak rock
and not as a soil
GEOLABS HAWAII
A large diameter 42 in observation shaft was placed at the Makiki
Park shaft location The shaft is cased with inspection windows and should
be available for inspection during bidding The contact between the
underlying clay and the overlying cinder sand was located at a depth of 54 4
to 2 ft below the excavated tunnel invert Water in the
shaft extended approximately 1 ft above the clay contact The cinder sand
exposed in the lower 10 ft the approximate tunnel interval was a clean
medium sized cinder sand slightly to uncemented which stood well in the wall
of the shaft A 2 in silt layer was present ft above the clay contact
and a 6 in silt layer was present 11 ft above the clay contact At higher
elevations in the shaft the cinders contained more silt and were often more
thinly bedded with size of the cinders varying from layer to layer The cin
ders stood well throughout the shaft depth but the experience with collapse
of cinders and low blow counts in several of the borings indicates that sec
tions of the tunnel will encounter cinder zones that will not stand vertically
in a tunnel face
Water is present in the cinders just above the fine grained marine and
volcanic sediments At the time of drilling the water level was 1 to 4 ft
below invert except in the borings near Stations 20 00 and 28 50 where the
water level was within the tunnel interval Near Station 20 00 the weathered

The cinder sand is expected to exhibit primarily firm to running behavior
For the most part the cinder sand should be stable in the tunnel face oar
ticularly where the cinders are cemented However running will occur in
uncemented cinders and some local ravelling may develop in cemented sections
These conditions can largely be controlled by a properly designed shield and
6 4
GEOLABS HAWAII
careful workmanship The and Associates 1971 study describes
little or no loosening of cinders above cracks in the existing sewer lining
along the Wilder Avenue portion of Reach 2 However uncemented cinders
caused hole collapse and drilling difficulties in Boring No G 10 Thus the
shield should be designed to support running soils in the face as well as to
excavate hard cemented cinders
Flowing conditions are expected to occur where the groundwater level is at
or above the tunnel invert or where perched water is present at tunnel level
Based on the present water levels flowing conditions are expected near
Station 20 00 Makiki Stream and Station Street Crossover but
could also occur anywhere along the alignment where silts and clays are in the
invert or if the general groundwater level rises to tunnel depth Rise in
groundwater level to the tunnel interval may occur sometime during the
construction period The most likely time would be from November to March
which is normally the rainy season The magnitude of the flowing problems
will depend in part on the presence of cementation in the cinder sand
Cemented cinders should not flow and should provide some face support whereas
uncemented cinders will flow rapidly from the face The lowest percentage of
cemented cinders encountered at tunnel level were in the borings located at
Makiki Stream and at Boring No G 10 near Punahou Street and Wilder Avenue
In addition perched water and wet zones were encountered in the borings
located near Makiki Stream and the Punahou Cliffs garden The stream bed was
dry during exploratory drilling Flowing conditions can be largely controlled
by dewatering within the tunnel using invert wells and controlled face
drainage In such a situation some delays should be anticipated It is
recommended that the water from the Punahou Cliffs garden be temporarily
drained prior to tunneling within 100 ft of the stream The quantity of water
inflow throughout Reach 2 is expected to be low

6 3 Mixed Volcanic Alluvial and Marine Section
Station 29 00 to Station 51461
Introduction
The section of sewer between the crossover and the east end of the pro
ject approximately 2260 L F will be driven along the southern edge of the
Rocky Hill volcanic cone and is located in a complex sequence of volcanic
alluvial mudflow and marine sediments and rocks The soil and rock con
ditions are highly variable and correlations between boreholes are extremely
tenuous This section will be the most difficult to construct because of the
large variability and potentially adverse ground conditions which range from
boulders and flowing ground to a full face of rock
The mixed section is divided into three reaches based primarily on the
presence of groundwater and the expected ground behavior Reach 3 is between
Reach 5 from Station 45 00 to 51 61 Drawing and 6 The expected
conditions and construction requiremants for each length are summarized in the
following sections
6 5
GEOLABS HAWAII
Mixed face rock and soil are expected along almost the full length of
Reach 3 The principal materials consist of a stiff to hard clay weakly
cemented and uncemented cinder sand with varying amounts of silt rock
basalt and hard cobbles and boulders Water is present in most of the
cinder layers and in the basalt
In order to view the soil and rock conditions directly a 42 in
diameter observation shaft was installed in the vicinity of Station 33 00
near boring G 14 The shaft is cased with windows cut for viewing and should
be made available for inspection by bidders prior to letting of the contract
Two basalt flows were encountered in the casing One of the flows does not
extend across the full width of the shaft and appears to have formed in a
narrow gully Thus the location and extent of the flows encountered in the
tunnel will be quite variable Zones of weathered tuff and a cinder zone
with silt were also encountered The materials in the shaft walls stood
without support Water was encountered on the marine clay at the bottom of
the shaft
1 Cinder Sand
Cinder sand is located in zones ranging from a few ft to 10 ft or
more in thickness Some zones are silty or cemented while other zones are
clean The elevation of the cinder zone is quite variable throughout the
reach
Flowing or running ground is expected where the tunnel is excavated
in uncemented cinder sand Most of the uncemented cinder sand should exhibit
flowing behavior running conditions are expected in local reaches and in sec
tions where the cinder sand is dewatered
The water in the cinder sand is typically perched above fine grained
marine and weathered tuff layers The source of the water appears to be from
groundwater inflow probably from Rocky Hill and possibly from leakage in the
6 7
GEOLABS HAWAII
existing sewer The presence of near surface groundwater is clearly evidenced
by the perennial spring located on the Punahou School property upslope of the
alignment The saturated thickness in the cinders is low varying from 2 to 6
ft and the cinder thickness and location of the cinder clay contact is extre
mely irregular Thus the cinder sand in this section will be difficult to
dewater and some water inflow should be expected even if closely spaced wells
are placed and pumped in advance of construction However it is recommended
that dewatering wells be installed to draw down water levels Dewatering
wells could initially be spaced on 20 to 40 ft centers and then spaced down
to 10 ft on center in areas where water and flowing cinders are encountered
Because of the low flows expected the wells would need to be submersible
with a vacuum
Flowing and running conditions are expected to occur in approximately 20
to 40 of Reach 3 One of the major problems in tunneling in Reach 3 is
unexpected development of flowing or running ground in the face during tunnel
advance Such conditions could occur anywhere along the reach and will be
most troublesome where the cinders are present in the arch or crown such as
near Boring No G 13 In the arch the flowing and running conditions will
cause loss of ground ahead of and above the tunnel face and may cause sub
sidence of the surface
Weak cementation of the cinder sand should help prevent flowing and
running conditions even where the cinders are water bearing However in the
mixed section cementation in the cinders is erratic both in degree and
occurrence and should not be relied on to prevent flowing and or running con
ditions
Feeler holes drilled ahead of the face should be enoloyed in the mixed
face section in order to locate rock soil and groundwater conditions

5 Marine Sediments
The marine deposits in Reach 4 consist basically of sand silt and

appear to be filled with very loose sand and silt The largest cavities and
voids appear to be close to the contact between the coral and the cinder sand

materials More extensive running behavior may develop where the reef is pri
marily unbonded sand and gravel fragments see Boring No G 18 Flowing con
ditions are not expected because the groundwater level is well below invert
Sections of the coral are hard enough that mechanical excavation such
as by diggers backhoes or hoe rams and perhaps blasting will be needed for
efficient excavation
The openwork nature and presence of very loose soils in the coral pose
foundation problems for support of the 9 foot diameter manhole SMH 7 near

founded on or just above the coral Excavation for the foundation should be

6 4 Control of Ground Movements
General
Tunneling and excavation should be carried out in such a way that
excessive movement or damage of pavements utilities structures and the
ground surface is prevented
The potential for ground movements can be evaluated by considering the
soil conditions anticipated and the sources of ground movement or ground loss
in and around the tunnel then evaluating the distribution of movements and
volume change in the soil mass and the resulting pattern of surface settle
ment and lateral displacement Finally the distortion of the structures can
be estimated and compared with damage or movement criteria
6 15
GEOLABS HAWAII
Sources of Ground Movement
Ground loss is dependent on the selected tunneling equipment and proce
dures and their compatibility with the soil water and rock conditions
existing along the alignment Further the skill of the work force in
carrying out the tunneling procedures will have a large impact on ground loss
both the average settlement and the potential for large localized loss of
ground
There are several potential sources of ground movement or ground loss
round a tunnel The ground loss is summarized in terms of the location of
its occurrence at the tunnel face around the tunnel shield around the
lining as it is installed at the tail of the shield in the case of a tunnel
advanced with a shield and around the lining after its installation
Often the largest ground losses take place into the face of the tunnel
when the support at the face is insufficient to hold the ground in place
Ground losses in the face may continue from shove to shove producing a regu
lar settlement pattern over the tunnel or they may occur suddenly and
locally resulting in a large and localized subsidence trough
Ground losses may develop around the tunnel shield when the excavated
perimeter is greater than the perimeter of the shield This can occur due to
the presence of poling plates overcutters or other protrusions on the
exterior of the shield that result in a larger cross sectional area at the
front of the shield than at the rear It may result from overexcavating out
side the shield perimeter at the tunnel face either by blasting or by mecha
nical or hand excavation Ground loss around the shield can also occur when
the body of the shield moves through the ground at an angle that is different
from the line or grade that the shield is following Tight radius curves and
shield configurations that make the shield difficult to steer or require
pitching the shield at a steeper angle than the grade in order to maintain
grade contribute to lost ground problems A shield that is short or is arti
culated is easier to maintain on line and grade and results in less ground
Loss
6 16
GEOLABS HAWAII
Ground losses often occur during installation of the tunnel lining if
the lining is not immediately grouted or expanded tightly against the
surrounding soil In a shield tunnel the installation of the lining takes
place in the tail of the shield and expansion or grouting of the lining takes
place as the lining emerges from the tail in order to fill the annular void
between the outside diameter of the shield and the outside diameter of the
lining
As the heading advances the installed lining takes load and will
deflect Usually the deflection is small with respect to the other ground
movements occurring around the tunnel However if the lining is not in good
contact with the ground on the side of the tunnel the deflections may be
significant in terms of their impact on settlement of the surrounding soil
In many soils most of the ground movement takes place as the tunnel is
advanced but long term movements may occur in cases where soft or disturbed
soils are subject to consolidation where soils can flow into the tunnel
through gaps in the initial lining or where voids formed during tunneling
later collapse

In the section from Station 0 00 to 29 00 Reaches 1 and 2 the
following ground conditions can occur

cinders

Support of the face is required but can be achieved by maintaining the
mack in the face at its angle of repose Use of breasting shelves would per
mit maltiple slopes to form at their angle of repose effectively steepening
the slope of the material in the face Ground loss in the face can be largely
prevented if this support is provided If the face were excavated vertically
without support and the tunnel passed from a self supporting face to a
running soil in the face then the volume of soil that would run into the
face before the natural angle of repose would choke off the run would be on
the order of
Combinations of harder cemented cinders or hard clay and looser
running cinders in the face can cause difficulties if the shield is not
capable of being shoved through the harder zones without excavating the face
vertically The looser cinders will run into the face unless the face can be
supported with breasting while cutting through the harder materials Progress
will be slowed if running is to be prevented in such a condition
Loss of ground around the shield and tail will occur rapidly in the
running ground loose uncemented cinders tending to fill the annular spaces
around the shield before they can be grouted

Table 6 2 Discussion
In Table 6 2 is outlined a procedure for estimating centerline surface
settlement Smax for given or assumed values of ground loss V at the
tunnel
The volume of the void around the tunnel that becomes filled with soil
Vu or the annulus A is linked to the maximum surface settlement Smay by
using the following relationships developed from experience on other pro
jects as well as from analyses and laboratory studies
The surface settlement volume Vs will be less than the Volume Vj of
lost ground because the soil above the tunnel increases in volume as movements
occur where AV is the volume change in the soil For a
given Volume of lost ground Vz the volume change in the soil will be greater
and the surface settlement volume smaller the deeper the tunnel and the denser
the soils Vs is estimated to range from 2 3 to
The settlement zone will extend outward on the surface to a point that can
be defined by a line inclined at an angle 8 from the vertical and extended
from the tunnel springline to the surface The distance from the centerline
is the half width w Substantial data has been obtained from actual field
measurements of the size of settlement troughs For sandy soils 8 values in
the range of 20 to 30 are typical A value of 26 5 was used in the example
Knowing both the surface settlement volume Vs and the half width w of
the trough permits the maximum settlement to be determined 0 ax Vs w
6 20
GEOLABS HAWAII
It is anticipated that at a tunnel depth of 50 ft to springline the
magnitude of surface settlement will be 1 in to 1 5 in for a 3 in annulus
loss At a tunnel depth of 25 ft to springline the same 3 in annulus loss
will produce a surface settlement of 2 to 3 in Measured deep settlement
would be about 10 in in this case In looser soils more movement will be
transmitted to surface in dense cemented soils it is quite likely that sur
face settlements would be negligible for a ground loss of 3 in annulus
around the tunnel
It is expected that shield tunneling with the face under control will
result in surface settlements of less than 2 in for tunnel depths of 40 ft or
more Additionally with careful control of the shield and with rapid and
complete tail void filling settlements of 1 in or less should be achievable
A loss of ground into the tunnel face of several cubic yards will not
immediately extend to the surface and thus can be arrested if the volume of
lost ground is replaced before tunneling is allowed to proceed
Ground Control Reguirements
Certain sections of the alignment will require tunneling with less
settlement than others
1 Crossing of the Freeway
It is recommended that settlement of the freeway be limited to less
than 1 in measured at the pavement or in the soil immediately below the
pavement The result would be 1 in in 25 ft or an average settlement slope
of 1 300 During tunneling beneath the freeway compaction replacement
grouting can be carried out through cased holes installed prior to tunneling
The low slump grout would be placed behind the tail of the shield as the tun
nel advances If large loss of ground occurs in the tunnel face then
grouting would be carried out over the shield to replace the lost ground
before the tunnel is advanced further Larger quantities of grout at lower
pressures would be required in this case than in the routine case where com
paction grout is placed behind the tail of the shield
6 21
GEOLABS HAWAII
2 Passage beneath existing sewer Wilder Avenue near Punahou Street
and Wilder Avenue at Piper s Pali
Because the proposed tunnel will pass only a few ft beneath the existing
sewer it will oe necessary to provide protection by diverting flow from the
existing sewer as discussed in Section by pumoing between manholes or
using a flume or pipe installed in the sewer
Passage beneath the existing sewer can be accomplished after a braced
excavation has been placed to expose and support the existing sewer or at
Wilder and Punahoa after consolidation grouting of the soils beneath and
beside the sewer has been accomplished to give the soils enough cohesion and
stiffness to be able to stand up around the tunnel
Monitoring of settlement of the existing sewer should be carried out as
the tunnel passes beneath it Monitoring points should be established on the
sewer crown by placing tell tales settlement points in the grout holes
drilled from the ground surface 10 ft on center over the crown Monitoring
points should also be established in the existing tunnel invert to monitor
settlement and separation of the invert slab Prior to putting the existing
sewer back in service it should be inspected and any damage developed during
tunneling repaired
3 Wilder Avenue

should not proceed until replacement grouting has been carried out
