The log of Hole CH 2 basically shows mixed soil and rock conditions
in and above the tunnel interval From a depth of 0 to 15 ft the soils
are silty sands and sandy silts with gravel cobbles and boulders above
a 6 ft thick layer of clayey silt weathered tuff A layer of rounded
cobbles and boulders alluvium was present at the base of the upper
unit The materials had sufficient cohesion so that the vertical side
walls were stable Some overexcavation occurred in the cobble layer
Two layers of cinder sand were encountered in the large diameter
hole the upper layer was between 15 and and the lower layer
between 28 5 and Both cinder layers were made up of medium to
coarse sand that was weakly cemented and friable The cinder sand was
moist but not saturated and did not exhibit running behavior in the
vertical shaft walls The upper cinder layer contains hard cobbles and
lies directly above a basalt flow The cobbles in the upper layer did not
cause excavation difficulties The lower cinder layer is underlain by and
lenses into a thick layer of marine clay and does not appear to be
hydraulically connected to the underlying basalt flow Thus dewatering
of some of the saturated cinder layers in Reach 3 using widely spaced
wells in the lava flows may not be completely effective and closely
spaced wells will likely be needed where the cinders are saturated
L 8
GEOLABS HAWAI
The stable behavior of the cinders in Shaft CH 2 should not be
expected throughout the entire length of Reaches 3 and 4 Moreover
flowing and or running ground should be expected where the cinder
layers are saturated or where the N values are low typically less
than or equal to 10 blows ft Ravelling ground is expected in the
cinder layers in and above the tunnel crown
Excavation of Test Hole CH 2 confirmed the presence of lava
flows in the mixed soil and rock sections of the alignment Two 4 to
5 ft thick lava flows were intersected in the hole at depths of 19 5 and
Plate L 2 The flows are continuous dip in a northeast to
southwest direction and appear to have originated from the Rocky Hill
vents The lava is made up of dark gray to black dense hard basalt
The basalt is slightly weathered to unweathered and moderately to closely
jointed Joint blocks are typically 0 5 to 1 ft in size but some cored
pieces are up to 3 ft in at least one dimension A broken clinker zone
was encountered at the bottom of the deepest basalt flow Clay seams were
present along some of the joints in the upper flow The lower flow will
be present from about springline to invert in the tunnel at the shaft
location The basalt flows were very difficult to drill and had to be
cored to complete the inspection hole
Weathered tuff and marine sediments along with a cinder sand layer
are present between the two lava flows The soils were excavated using the
42 in diameter auger Cobbles and boulders in the tuff and marine soils
caused some difficulty and delay in excavation but the hole was much more
rapidly advanced as compared with drilling in rock Plate L 2 The clay
was stable in the vertical shaft walls and did not ravel even where it was
fissured and slickensided between 30 5 and 35 ft However ravelling con
ditions are expected where the clays are present in and above the tunnel
perimeter
On the groundwater table was encountered at a depth
of 37 ft Some flowing and sloughing occurred in the broken clinker
zone at the bottom of the hole
L 9
GEOLABS HAWAII
L 4 General Discussion of Shaft Conditions
The large diameter shafts excavated for this project provide an
excellent opportunity to observe the in place character and behavior of
the materials along portions of the proposed alignment Prospective
bidders should be encouraged to examine the materials exposed in the
casing windows It must be remembered that the materials at the shafts
are not completely representative of all the materials along the align
ment particularly east of Station 29 00 Furthermore the soils and
rocks in the vertical shaft walls are generally more stable than the
same materials in tunnel face and around the tunnel perimeter Difficult
tunneling conditions as described in Section 6 3 should be expected in
Reaches 3 and 4 of the proposed sewer line

APPENDIX M
GROUT INJECTION TESTS
APPENDI X M
Grout Injection Tests
M1 Introduction
Grout injection tests were performed in two borings one located
near the Punahou Street crossover Boring G 39 and the second near the
crossover at Piper s Pali Boring G 34 Drawing Nos 4 and 5 The
purpose of the tests was to determine the groutability of the cinder
sand and coral units at various consistencies of neat cement grout
Test locations were chosen in two locations where cement grout may be
useful in stabilizing the cinders in the crossover area for the
tunneling option and to fill voids in the coral to provide an adequate
foundation for shafts which were subsequently deleted In addition
grouting tests in the second boring were performed in a thin layer of
loose cinder sand above the coral Test procedures and results are
presented in the following paragraphs
M 2 Equipment
The grouted zones in both test borings were drilled using a 4 in
I D steel casing which was advanced by washing and rotational downward
pressure drilled in casing The drilling was accomplished in Boring
G 39 using a CME 45 exploratory drill rig and Boring G 34 using a Mobil
B 34 rig The drilled in casing method provided clean holes for
injection of the grout so that washing prior to pressure testing was not
needed
Pressure testing and grout injection were accomplished using the
pumps on the drill rigs The pumps are variable speed centrifical
pumps the pump used to grout Boring G 39 has an operating speed of 190
to 400 RPM and a maximum operating pressure of 225 psi The grout was
mixed in two 14 et grout mixing tubs equipped with 6 mixing paddles
M 1
GEOLABS HAWAIli
The paddles were driven using a 263 CFM Atlas Copco air compressor
After the grout was mixed it was dropped into a 12 et mud tub below
the batching plant and was then pumped into the borehole
The grout injection system was made up of the pump grout lines
header packer assembly and mud tub The grout lines were set up to
inject into the hole and or to return to the mud tub return line
system The header contained a pressure gage and valves for operating
the injection and return lines The packer assembly had a 30 in long
inflatable packer and a 5 ft long perforated grout pipe which was
located below the base of the packer The packer was inflated to 400
psi and the grout holes in the grout pipes were 3 8 in diameter The
grout operation is shown in Photograph M 1
M 3 Drilling and Grouting Procedures
The grouting operation was carried out from the top down i e
stage grouting procedure typically in 10 foot intervals The zone to
be grouted was sampled and then the casing advanced In Boring G 39
standard split spoon samples were taken in the cinder sand and in Boring
_ G 34 the coral was cored with a Trifus triple tube core barrel Cored
samples of cinder sand similar to grouted sands in Boring G 39 were
obtained in Boring G 13 which is located approximately 250 ft from the
grout test hole No cored samples were taken of the loose cinder sand
above the coral in Boring G 34 Sieve analyses were performed on
representative samples from each grout hole see Appendix E
After the casing was drilled to the bottom of the grout zone the
casing was pulled up so that the shoe was at the top of the zone Plate
M 2 The packer assembly was then set so that the mid point of the
packer was located at the bottom of the casing This procedure allowed
the top of the grouted zone to be sealed both in soil or rock and in the
casing In this way leaks around the casing were minimized or
M 2
GEOLABS HAWAII
prevented The top of the casing was sealed at the surface with rags
and or bentonite pellets The final step was the grout assembly hookup
The grouting procedure basically involved water pressure testing
and then injection of neat cement grout of successively thicker mixes
lower water cement ratios Injection was generally made at or below
maximum gage pressures equal to the overburden depth in psi above the
top of the grouted zone or where surface leakage occurred equivalent to
the fluid weight of the column of water or grout When surface leakage
occurred the pressure and flow were held relatively constant by
maintaining the pool level in the depression around the casing The
initial grout mix had a water cement ratio of 7 1 and the second mix was
typically The third and sometimes fourth mix had water cement
ratios in the range of 2 1 to 1 1 In general one batch 7 2
typically of each mix was injected in the grout zone stage Care was
taken to prevent premature grout refusal by providing a continuous flow
of grout to the hole
Pressure testing and then grouting were started by first
recirculating the fluid grout valve closed and return valve open and
then by slowly opening the down line Once the down or grout line was
fully open then the return line was slowly closed up to the point where
maximum pressure was reached or a surface leak developed Surface leaks
were sealed or the grout water level maintained at a constant level
Washing of the cinders was attempted only in the upper level zone
State I of Boring G 39 The wash pipe was a 5 ft section of
perforated A size drill rod Water was injected using the drilling pump
operating at an estimated discharge of 10 to 20 gpm The washing was
set up to clean 3 to 5 ft intervals over periods of 5 minutes however
the hole caved even though the cinders were cemented Washing
operations were terminated for subsequent stages because of potential
collapse and because the drilling return water was clean Based on the
GEOLABS HAWAII
test results all grout holes should be drilled using drilled in casing
or coring with water to remove the cuttings Other drilling methods
such as air rotary or drilling mud procedures should not be allowed
because of possible coating the sides of the hole reduced or no grout
take and because of potential difficulties with hole collapse during
washing The first stage of Test Hole G 39 was redrilled prior to
grouting
M 4 Test Results
M Street Crossover Boring G 39
M General
Injection of grout in Boring G 39 was done in 3 stages or
zones aS shown in Fig M 2 The test hole was located between the
existing and proposed sewers and was drilled roughly from the
inside wall of the existing tunnel Zone I was drilled and grouted from
depths of 22 to 32 ft and was located from 10 ft above to the crown of
the existing sewer Zone II depth 32 to 42 ft covered the interval
from the top of the existing sewer down to a point approximately midway
between the two tunnels and Zone III was within the proposed sewer
interval depth 42 to 51 ft The test hole was advanced by augering to
a depth of 10 ft and then by drilling in casing from 10 to the bottom of
the hole 51 ft
M Soil Conditions
The soil conditions adjacent to the test hole are shown in
the summary cross section Plate M 1 and in the log of Boring G 39
Appendix B From a depth of 0 to the soil is a very stiff to
hard low permeability silty clay weathered tuff with sand and gravel
disseminated in the clay matrix Between 11 5 and 28 ft the soil
GEOLABS HAWAII
consists of cinder sand and interbedded cinder sand and silt In the
upper 7 ft of Zone I the soil is primarily interbedded cinder sand and
silt with silt layers typically 0 1 to thick and spaced 0 3 to 1
ft apart The lower 3 ft of Zone I is clean weakly cemented cinder
sand The cinder sand throughout Zone I is a fine to coarse sand with
about 5 fine gravel and 2 to 3 passing the No 200 sieve The di
size is fine sand range and the uniformity coefficient is 6
Comparison of the gradation curves shows that the distribution
characteristics of the cinder sand is essentially the same where the
cinders are clean and where the cinders are interbedded with silt
Zone II was located at a depth of 32 to 42 ft almost entirely in
fine to coarse weakly cemented to uncemented cinder sand Fig M 3 N
values ranged between 18 and 30 blows ft medium dense One thin silty
layer approximately 8 fines was present at a depth of 35 ft Zone
III was grouted between 42 and 51 ft The upper 3 ft of the zone was in
clean cinders but below 45 ft the cinders were weathered oxidized and
slightly silty The base of the cinder sand was at where a very
stiff low permeability silty clay was encountered at the bottom of the
boring The interval between 45 and is the range of ground
water level fluctuations
M Grout Injection Test Results
Results of the water pressure and grout injection tests for the 3
grout stages in Test Hole G 39 are summarized in Plates M 1 to M 7 The
test results clearly show that the cinder sand can take neat cement
grout in water cement ratios ranging between 7 1 to 1 1 by weight
takes were in Zones II and III which were predominately clean cinder
sand The gage pressure was 0 psi during injection of all the mixes in
zones II and III The lowest grout takes were in Zone I which was made
up principally of interbedded cinders and silt In Zone I refusal was
GEOLABS HAWAII
almost reached during injection of the mix and was obtained 0
grout take in 5 minutes when the mix was thickened to a water cement
ratio of 1 1 Moreover grout takes were low even during injection of
the 7 1 mix Based on the test hole samples most of the grout injected
into Zone I probably was into the clean cinder sand in the lower 4 ft of
th stage
M Summary and Recommendations
Based on the grout test results we have concluded that the clean
cinder sand can be grouted with neat cement mixes from 3 ft above the
existing tunnel to the invert of the proposed tunnel in the Punahou
Street Crossover area Recommend grouting materials to include chemical
grout consisting of sodium silicate and cement All grout holes must be
drilled by water coring or washed and drilled in casing Surface leaks
may be a problem and adequate surface seals such as with bentonite dry
pack cement etc must be placed prior to grouting
The test results also revealed that cement grout cannot be
effectively injected into the interbedded cinder and silt deposits
Thus grout stabilization is not recommended for sections of tunnel in
Reach 1 such as the crossing beneath Highway H l
M General
Injection of grout in Boring G 34 was carried out in 3 stages
or zones aS shown on Plate M 9 to M 15 The test hole was located
approximately 25 feet west of the crossover Zone I was drilled and
grouted from depths of 21 0 to 23 0 feet and was located at the crown of
the proposed tunnel excavation Zone II depth 24 5 to 34 5 feet
covered the interval from near the crown to about 7 5 feet below the
M 6
GEOLABS HAWAII
proposed tunnel excavation Zone III was 7 5 to 14 0 feet beneath the
proposed tunnel excavation and sewer manhole foundation level 35 0 to
41 0 feet The first 25 feet of the test hole was advanced by augering
with continuous split spoon sampling A 4 inch diameter drilled in
casing was then installed to a depth of 25 feet From 25 0 to 45 0 feet
bottom of hole the hole was advanced by coring with a Triefus triple
tube core barrel The drilling fluid was water
M Soil Conditions
The soil conditions adjacent to the test hole are shown in the
summary cross section Plate M 9 and in the log of Boring G 34
Appendix B From a depth of 0 to 21 0 feet the soil consists of
interbedded silty clay basalt lava flows and boulders silty fine sand
beach sand silt alluvium and black coarse to medium sand with silt
cinder Zone I was located between 21 0 to 23 0 feet and made up of a
layer of black coarse to medium cinder sand with about 10 silt Plate
placed in the cinder and underlying coral reef contact area prior to
grout injection in Zone I
zone It was located at a depth of 24 5 to 34 5 feet almost
entirely in cemented coral which is jointed and contains cavities in
local areas 34 5 to 35 5 feet Zone III was grouted between 35 0 to
40 0 feet because the gravel and cobble sized coral fragments
encountered were unstable and caved in after the drilled in casing was
contains both cemented coral and uncemented gravel sized coral fragments

GEOLABS HAWAII
M Grout Injection Test Results
Results of the water pressure and grout injection tests for the
3 grout stages in Test Hole G 34 are summarized on Plates M 9 to M 15
The test results obtained in Zone I show that the grout takes in loose
Refusal occurred during initial injection of the mix 0 grout take
in 20 minutes
The largest 0 65 and 1 08 sacks foot and fastest
approximately 17 6 and 14 4 sacks hour grout takes were in Zones II
and III respectively which were in coral reef deposits Based on the
test hole samples most of the grout injected into Zone II probably went
into cavities near the bottom of Zone II and in the uncemented and
open work coral fragments in the upper 4 feet of Zone III The maximum
gage pressure was 8 psi which occurred during injection of the 2 1
cement grout mix in Zone II
No grout or water return occurred around the outside of the
casing at the ground surface
M Summary and Recommendations
Based on the grout test results the coral reef materials at
the vicinity of the test site can be grouted with neat cement mixes to a
minimum depth of 15 feet beneath the tunnel invert Grout holes should
be drilled by coring or washed and drilled in casing Surface leaks may
be a problem and adequate surface seals such as with bentonite dry
pack cement etc should be placed prior to grouting
The test results also revealed that cement grout cannot be
effectively injected into cinder sand that contains a significant amount
of silt
